## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, combining elastic/plastic deformation mechanics with thermal softening effects. Stress typically increases with strain (hardening) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic deformation)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress offset)
- Ramberg-Osgood (inverted form): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * epsilon (combined linear and power-law terms)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturation hardening model)
- Temperature-dependent power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated flow with hardening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Swift equation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (1 - c3 * T) (shifted power law with linear softening)
- Hyperbolic sine flow law: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep law, inverted)
- Polynomial with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (quadratic hardening with linear thermal factor)
- Exponential thermal softening with hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (Arrhenius-type temperature dependence combined with hardening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening (concave-down stress-strain curve) → Power-law form epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or saturation form (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening (stress decreases with temperature) → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**n) or exp(-c*T)
- Yield stress offset (nonzero stress intercept at small strain) → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon)
- Separable strain-temperature dependence → Product form f(epsilon) * g(T), common in Johnson-Cook type models
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as ratio T/T_melt, modeled as (1 - c*T) with c absorbing melting point
- Strain saturation behavior → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) approaching asymptotic stress
- Rate-independent plasticity transition → Piecewise or smooth transition near yield: c0*epsilon for small epsilon transitioning to power law
- Creep/thermally activated deformation → sinh or exp(c/T) terms coupling strain rate effects with temperature
